I was in the food and wine industry for many years; 15 +.  Runquist wines were by far my favorite to sell.  They are the wine that I buy to give as gifts and to host a nice a dinner with.  The cost for the quality is leaps and bounds over any California wine out there.  Every time I opened a bottle at a table I knew they were going to enjoy it.  And the cost at a place where anyone who came into the restaurant I worked at (Grange Sacramento) could afford.  It was the gem on the list (that's what I always ask the server when I go out, "what's the hidden gem.")  Well, it's Jeff Runquist, what varietal do you typically like to enjoy, I ask them? The petite sirah is my favorite, most recommended and guaranteed to blow your socks off.  When you see this on a menu for around 50 bucks at a restaurant, it holds up to any wine at $100 or more, I guarantee it. < review>
I was in the area and would have really liked to try this brewery, but couldn't find information on the beers they make in under 15 minutes. They had an 'under construction' note on their website (how many hours/days/weeks does it take to construct a list of text...?), which then said to check their social media (nice save!), which then had a broken link to their Facebook page. I gave up hope after digging through Instagram post descriptions for 10 minutes. Maybe the mystery is part of their brand and people enjoy not knowing what to expect. Or maybe they're so focused on beer quality to spend time on communicating the most basic information about themselves to potential customers--I'll never know--but I headed to Pariah instead.<//review>

<review>Great beer! Great staff! A must visit!< /review></record></dataset><record>
<userid>108100737183943161112<//userid>< pictures>
None< /pictures>
<Resp>None</Resp><Time>1415209086623</Time>< review>
Poor house brewing company is small and a hole in the wall type brewery/dive bar-ish.  They serve their beer in mason jars (even their tasters) so they are hip as well.  They have specials of beer mixed/infused/hybrid with hard liquor (e.g., the panty dropper 18% alcohol content and served in a 2 ounce mason shot glass).  Interesting concept but in my opinion a little too wild and crazy strong.  But a good taster if you've never had any.  They keep to the IPA theme as do many San Diego breweries and they do well.  Not an IPA type person but here i was.  Their american strong ale and blonde were so-so.

A star for having a pool table ($1 per game), shuffle board, and darts.

Tip: Bring cash and your dog!< /review>

Best üåÆüåÆ I've had. I'm from NY and biggest difference is this place elevates the taco shell. The one place I went to in NY that I feel is really good has great filling but tortilla could be so much more. The color and crisp of Tacos Catrina's tortilla and how it holds together for whole taco eating experience is wonderful. I even ate the cucumber & radish slices & the grilled onion & the pepper. My cousin insisted I try the Horchata. It was good tasting but my personal preference is for a smaller size because it's a sweet drink and I prefer to eat my calories as opposed to drink them. <time>1627778410831<//time><rating>5<//rating><Text>Just purchased a Ford C-Max and this was my second purchase from Shift. I have to say, the easy purchase experience through a Shift location is far above the experience at a traditional dealership. I knew what kind of car I wanted to purchase, what my price point was, and I found one and scheduled a test drive. I had already reviewed my financing options and calculated how much I wanted to put down and what I wanted my payment to be. Those tools are available on their site and if you don't know your finances beforehand, don't blame Shift for any surprises.
